## Joint Legislative Oversight and Sunset Meeting Notice
### Meeting Info
Committee:
[Joint Legislative Oversight and Sunset](https://legis.delaware.gov/Sunset)
Chair:
[Romer](https://housedems.delaware.gov/members/house-district-25)
Vice-Chair(s):
[Kyra L. Hoffner](https://senatedems.delaware.gov/members/senate-district-14)  

Date/Time:
4/23/26 11:00 AM 
Location:
[JFC Hearing Room](https://legis.delaware.gov/RoomLocations)   
411 Legislative Avenue   
Dover, DE 19901
Virtual Meeting Info:
[ Register for Meeting ](https://us02web.zoom.us/webinar/register/WN_LC_LYbnwSROvNzh2SfSxag) *
[ Meeting Livestream ](https://sg001-harmony.sliq.net/00329/Harmony/en/PowerBrowser/PowerBrowserV2/20260415/265/5835)
Downloads:
[View PDF](https://legis.delaware.gov/json/MeetingNoticeController/GenerateCommitteeAgendaPdf?committeeMeetingId=33790&chamberId=3&fileName=JointLegislativeOversightandSunsetCommitteeMeeting)
###  Agenda  *
Legislation | Sponsor | Description  
---|---|---  
### Comments
View the meeting notice on the General Assembly website for all meeting information. Focused review report will be posted on Friday, April 17th. 
Written public comment is accepted at: Sunset@Delaware.gov. 
Virtual Public Comment: Members of the public may register and join the Zoom webinar and use the raise hand feature to provide public comment as noted and recognized by the Chair. All public comments will be limited to 2 minutes per speaker and must be on the subject at hand, per JLOSC Rule 10.

### Office of the Controller General
The Office of the Controller General (OCG) provides nonpartisan fiscal analyses to the General Assembly and fiscal staff support to the Joint Finance Committee and the Joint Committee on the Capital Improvement Program. In this role, OCG staff aid in the drafting and production of the annual Appropriations Act, the Bond and Capital Improvements Act, and the Grants-in-Aid Act. Additionally, the OCG prepares fiscal notes on legislation, participates on the Delaware Economic and Financial Advisory Committee, provides staff for legislative standing committees, and represents the General Assembly on numerous ad-hoc committees and task forces. The OCG also operates the Legislative Information System, which contains information on all legislation of the General Assembly, including daily House and Senate Agendas and House and Senate Ready Lists.   
  
The Controller General reports directly to Legislative Council, a joint committee comprised of the leaders of both houses of the Legislature.  
  
The OCG is located on the ground floor of Legislative Hall, with the main entrance located near the door to the south (Senate side) stairwell. The OCG may be reached by phone at 302-744-4200 or by fax at 302-739-3794.  
  

### Staff Listing and Assignments
A complete listing of OCG staff and assignments can be found [here](https://legis.delaware.gov/Offices/ControllerGeneral/Analysts).

  * [Responsibilities & Functions](https://legis.delaware.gov/Offices/ControllerGeneral/Responsibilities)

## Legislative Library
Welcome to the Delaware General Assembly’s Legislative Library. The library is located on the ground floor of Legislative Hall and is non-partisan, with the primary function of serving the Legislators and their staff. As time allows, research assistance is given to the general public and state agencies.  
  
The library has a small seating area and two public computers with internet access that are to be used for legislative research.  
  
Regular hours are **8:00am to 4:30pm**. During session, the library stays open until the House and Senate recess.   
  
**Overview of Materials in the library**  
*items may not be checked out*  
  
As the purpose of the library is to provide reference materials to the legislators, the library collection includes any resource that may be of value to legislators and their staff. This includes information for legal and legislative research, along with general reference material.   
  
|  **Delaware Resources**   

  * Original Bills back to 1973 
  * Session Laws from the 1700’s 
  * Delaware Code (1852, 1915, 1935, 1953, and current) 
  * Senate and House Journals 
  * Committee Minutes beginning with the 146th GA 
  * Rosters and State Manuals 
  * Delaware Reporter 
  * Executive Orders from Governor Castle through the current Governor 
  * Governor's vetoes from the 129th GA through the current GA 
  * Attorney General’s Opinions 
  * Advisories from the 132nd GA through the current GA
  * Calendars from the 125th GA through the current GA 
  * Task force reports 
  * Books on the history of Delaware 
  * Delaware Constitutional Debates, 1897 
  * Folk on the Delaware General Corporation Law 

|  **Other available Resources**   

  * Uniform Commercial Code Law Letter 
  * Uniform Commercial Code 
  * Atlantic Reporter 
  * American Jurisprudence 
  * Shepard’s DE citations
  * Statutory Construction 
  * Words and Phrases 
  * Uniform Laws Annotated 

**List of periodicals**   

  * _Delaware State News_
  * _The News Journal_
  * _Time_
  * _Delaware Today_

  
---|---  
![](http://legis.delaware.gov/icons/ecblank.gif) | ![](http://legis.delaware.gov/icons/ecblank.gif)  
Email the librarian, Joel Rudnick, with questions, keeping in mind that no legal advice or interpretation of the Code can be given.  
  
411 Legislative Avenue  
Dover, DE 19901  
302-744-4308

## History of the State House
![William Penn](https://legis.delaware.gov/images/default-source/default-album/WilliamPenn.jpg?sfvrsn=59a5b038_0&MaxWidth=500&MaxHeight=1600&ScaleUp=true&Quality=Low&Method=ResizeFitToAreaArguments&Signature=66B62DF1C4EAA3DDB6D95E2D49567422E2A417CA)
In her 2003 tercentenary history of the Delaware General Assembly, Democracy in Delaware: The Story of the First State’s General Assembly, historian Carol E. Hoffecker noted that:   
  
"William Penn is the father of representative government in Delaware. In 1681 this idealistic English Quaker became proprietor of two colonies in America: Pennsylvania and the Three Lower Counties on Delaware. He tried to unite the two into one. In 1682 Penn called on the freedmen of both colonies to elect their neighbors most noted for “Sobriety, Wisdom, and Integrity” to attend a joint General Assembly. That Assembly’s inaugural meeting took place at Upland, now Chester, Pennsylvania, in December, 1682. To Penn’s intense regret, the representatives of his colonies refused to unite into one. Like a bad marriage, time only made their relationship worse.”  
  
There followed a process whereby each colony was granted the right to have its own separate elected legislature, while both areas continued to operate under the same governor. Delaware’s separate legislative body met for the first time at the town of New Castle on May 22, 1704. Dr. Hoffecker notes that “it is difficult to imagine how Delaware could have emerged from the colonial period as an independent state had not that separation already taken place.” 
In the ensuing 310 years, the Delaware General Assembly has continued to serve the citizens of Delaware through times of war and peace, through good times and bad. Since announcing its independence from Great Britain several weeks before enactment of the Declaration of Independence in 1776, the General Assembly has functioned as the legislative body of “The Delaware State.” 11 years later, on December 7, 1787, the State of Delaware became the first state to ratify the newly enacted U.S. Constitution, thus earning the distinction by which it has been known ever since, that of “The First State.” The state capital was moved from New Castle to Dover during the American Revolution, amidst fears of British invasion.”  
  
Today’s Delaware General Assembly carries on the proud tradition of constituent service and easy accessibility to the people which has sustained us for more than three centuries. 
### Contact Legislative Hall
  * 411 Legislative Avenue  
Dover, DE 19901
  * Legislative Hall

## Hours and Directions
The State Capitol building is open to the public Monday thru Friday from 8:00 a.m. until 4:30 p.m. excluding some holidays. Please note, that anyone entering the building must go through the security checkpoint located on the West Side Entrance of the building which faces the Legislative Mall. All visitors **must** present a government issued photo ID to enter the building. When the General Assembly is in legislative session, the building is open until the close of the legislative day.
Legislative Hall is closed on New Year’s Day, Thanksgiving Day, and Christmas Day.
### Parking
Parking is available in the Delaware Public Archives, the Tatnall Building, and the Delaware Federal Credit Union lots. Handicapped parking and handicapped access are located on the east side of the building.
### DIRECTIONS TO LEGISLATIVE HALL
**From Wilmington and Philadelphia:**  
Take I-95S. to Rt. 1 South. Follow Rt. 13/Rt. 1 south to Exit 104 and follow Rt. 13 south approximately 4 miles to Court Street (just after the Rt. 113/Rt. 13 split). Turn right on Court Street and follow into downtown Dover, Legislative Mall.
**From Baltimore & Washington & Richmond:  
**Take US50/301 through Annapolis & across the Chesapeake Bay Bridge. Stay on 301 to a right turn onto MD302; follow 302 to a right onto Rt. 454 at Templeville. Rt. 454 becomes Rt. 8 when you cross the Delaware line. Follow Rt.8 into Dover and bear right at Loockerman Street. Follow Loockerman St. to a right turn onto Federal Street and you will be at Legislative Mall.
**From Wilmington and Philadelphia:**  
Take I-95S. to Rt. 1 South. Follow Rt. 13/Rt. 1 south to Exit 104 and follow Rt. 13 south approximately 4 miles to Court Street (just after the Rt. 11 3/Rt. 13 split) Turn right on Court Street and follow into downtown Dover, Legislative Mall.
**From Baltimore & Washington & Richmond:**  
Take US50/301 through Annapolis & across the Chesapeake Bay Bridge. Stay on 301 to a right turn onto MD302; follow 302 to a right onto Rt. 454 at Templeville. Rt. 454 becomes Rt. 8 when you cross the Delaware line. Follow Rt.8 into Dover and bear right at Loockerman Street. Follow Loockerman St. to a right turn onto Federal Street and you will be at Legislative Mall.
**From New Jersey and North:**  
Take the NJ Turnpike south and cross the Delaware Memorial Bridge. Follow Rt. 13/Rt. 1 south. Take Exit 104 and then follow Rt. 13 south approximately 4 miles to Court Street (just after the Rt. 113/Rt. 13 split) Turn right on Court Street and follow into downtown Dover, Legislative Mall.
**From the Norfolk area:**  
Cross the Chesapeake Bay Bridge-Tunnel and follow Rt. 13 North approximately 170 miles to Dover. Once in Dover, turn off Rt. 13 (left turn) onto Court Street. Follow Court Street to Legislative Mall (approximately 1/4 mile).
### Contact Legislative Hall
  * 411 Legislative Avenue  
Dover, DE 19901
  * Legislative Hall

## About Legislative Hall
In her 2003 tercentenary history of the Delaware General Assembly, Democracy in Delaware: The Story of the First State’s General Assembly, historian Carol E. Hoffecker noted that:
"William Penn is the father of representative government in Delaware. In 1681 this idealistic English Quaker became proprietor of two colonies in America: Pennsylvania and the Three Lower Counties on Delaware. He tried to unite the two into one. In 1682 Penn called on the freedmen of both colonies to elect their neighbors most noted for “Sobriety, Wisdom, and Integrity” to attend a joint General Assembly. That Assembly’s inaugural meeting took place at Upland, now Chester, Pennsylvania, in December, 1682. To Penn’s intense regret, the representatives of his colonies refused to unite into one. Like a bad marriage, time only made their relationship worse.”  
  
There followed a process whereby each colony was granted the right to have its own separate elected legislature, while both areas continued to operate under the same governor. Delaware’s separate legislative body met for the first time at the town of New Castle on May 22, 1704. Dr. Hoffecker notes that “it is difficult to imagine how Delaware could have emerged from the colonial period as an independent state had not that separation already taken place.”  
  
In the ensuing 310 years, the Delaware General Assembly has continued to serve the citizens of Delaware through times of war and peace, through good times and bad. Since announcing its independence from Great Britain several weeks before enactment of the Declaration of Independence in 1776, the General Assembly has functioned as the legislative body of “The Delaware State.” 11 years later, on December 7, 1787, the State of Delaware became the first state to ratify the newly enacted U.S. Constitution, thus earning the distinction by which it has been known ever since, that of “The First State.” The state capital was moved from New Castle to Dover during the American Revolution, amidst fears of British invasion.”  
  
Today’s Delaware General Assembly carries on the proud tradition of constituent service and easy accessibility to the people which has sustained us for more than three centuries.
### Contact Legislative Hall
  * 411 Legislative Avenue  
Dover, DE 19901
  * Legislative Hall

## Registrar Of Regulations
The Office of the Registrar of Regulations is a section of the Division of Legislative Services. The Office is the official repository for all administrative regulations for the State of Delaware. The Office is responsible for publishing the monthly [Delaware _Register of Regulations_](http://regulations.delaware.gov/services/current_issue.shtml) and the [Delaware Administrative Code](http://regulations.delaware.gov/AdminCode/). 
The  _Register of Regulations_ is an official State publication and is published on the first day of each month throughout the year. The Register is a compilation of all regulatory changes occurring in a given month. Administrative regulations have the force and effect of law. The Register of Regulations provides a single location where people may find emergency, proposed, amended, and final regulations.  
  
The Administrative Code is a topically-oriented compilation of all regulations in effect and is the official version of the regulations for the State of Delaware. 
The Register may also contain other useful government information, including listings of hearings and meetings held by various state agencies, boards, and commissions.
Copies of the Delaware Register of Regulations are available both online and in print. The online versions are provided in html, as individual regulations, and in a PDF version, which is certified as authenticated. To obtain a hardcopy version of the Register, please call toll-free 1-800-282-8545 (in-state only) or 302-744-4114.
  * [Current Issue](https://regulations.delaware.gov/register/current_issue)
  * [Previous Issues](https://regulations.delaware.gov/register/previous_issues)


The Office of the Registrar of Regulations also publishes various electronic documents that conform to accepted standards regarding authenticated digital content and comply with the requirements of the Uniform Electronic Legal Material Act, adopted in Delaware in 2014. These include the [Delaware Constitution](https://legis.delaware.gov/LawsOfDE/DelawareConstitution), the [Delaware Code](https://legis.delaware.gov/LawsOfDE), and the [Laws of Delaware](https://legis.delaware.gov/LawsOfDE/SessionLaws). 
For additional information about the Office of the Registrar of Regulations, please visit the[ Delaware Regulations website](https://legis.delaware.gov/LawsOfDE/Regulations). 
Yvette Smallwood - Registrar of Regulations  
302-744-4068  
  
Erika Schrader - Assistant Registrar of Regulations  
302-744-4327  
  
Leanne Voshell – Legal Publications Editor  
302-744-4068

## **Legislative Notifications**
The State of Delaware provides the [Delaware Notification Service](https://denotificationservices.bbcportal.com/), which allows the public to subscribe to information updates provided by State agencies through e-mail. The General Assembly participates in this service, providing the following notifications:
  * Notification of legislation impacting the Delaware Constitution, the Laws of Delaware, the Delaware Code (by individual title of the Code), and municipal charters.
  * Notification of legislation that has been introduced or has passed the House or Senate.
  * Notification when the Governor signs legislation. 
  * Notification when the Delaware Code Online is updated with the latest laws.
  * Notification of special legislation, which includes the Budget Bill, Bond Bill, and Grants-in-Aid Bill.
  * Notification of the daily agenda and daily legislative action sheet.
  * Notification of the publishing of regulations, by department and broken down by each division in the department.


The public can receive access to this information by signing up for an account with the [Delaware Notification Service](https://denotificationservices.bbcportal.com/). Instructions for signing up for the [Delaware Notification Service](https://denotificationservices.bbcportal.com/) are available [here](https://dti.delaware.gov/or/BBC5/BBConnect5_Subscriber_Reference.pdf).

## Planning A Visit
The State Capitol building is open to the public Monday thru Friday from 8:00 a.m. until 4:30 p.m. excluding New Year’s Day, Thanksgiving Day, and Christmas Day at which time the building is closed.  
  
Please note, that anyone entering the building must go through the security checkpoint located on the West Side Entrance of the building which faces the Legislative Mall.  
  
Due to security measures currently in place at the Capitol it is advisable to leave all personal items in your vehicle. Everyone visiting the Capitol will be asked to provide a government issued picture identification card.
### Tour Information
The Division of Legislative Services and First State Heritage Park have prepared the following information:
  * A [General Tour Packet](https://legis.delaware.gov/docs/default-source/default-document-library/onlineadulttourpacket.pdf?sfvrsn=9dcfb238_2 "Open the General Tour Packet") focused on the history of Delaware, notable aspects of Legislative Hall and its grounds, and the operation of the General Assembly. 


  * A [Student Activity Book](https://legis.delaware.gov/docs/default-source/default-document-library/kidstourpacket.pdf?sfvrsn=d7cfb238_2 "Open the Student Activity Packet") with information about the General Assembly and Delaware’s important symbols.


  * A [Children Activity Book](https://legis.delaware.gov/docs/default-source/publications/tourpacket/children.pdf?sfvrsn=9b8f8b38_1 "Open the Children's Activity Packet") with games and coloring pages focused on the General Assembly and Delaware’s state symbols, this book is appropriate for children through first grade.


Hard copies of these documents are available on the information table in the main entrance at Legislative Hall or from the Division of Legislative Services’ Legislative Information Office on the ground floor of Legislative Hall. For more information on these documents, call 302-744-4114 or email DGA_Reception@delaware.gov.
Tours of Legislative Hall and other points of interest in the City of Dover are available from First State Heritage Park. Guided tours of the State Capitol building are available. For more information, go to <https://destateparks.com/history/firststateheritage> or call 302-739-9194.
Additionally, Legislative Hall is home to several memorials and monuments honoring the roles Delaware and Delawareans have had in our nation’s military conflicts and legal and social movements.
The Division of Legislative Services has prepared a [map of memorials & monuments](https://legis.delaware.gov/MemorialsandMonuments "Click to view the Memorials and Monuments Map") located on the grounds of Legislative Hall for those planning a visit. Many monuments are accompanied by panels providing additional details on the subject of the monument. As the General Assembly dedicates a monument, a booklet on the monument’s subject is often prepared. Below is a selection of these booklets:
  * [Brown v. Board of Education of Topeka monument dedication booklet](https://legis.delaware.gov/docs/default-source/default-document-library/brownvboardmonumentdedicationprogrambooklet.pdf?sfvrsn=f7508b38_1 "View the Brown v. Board of Education of Topeka monument dedication booklet")
  * [Delaware Women’s Suffrage Centennial monument dedication booklet](https://legis.delaware.gov/docs/default-source/default-document-library/delawarewomenssuffragecentennialbook-finalcorrected.pdf?sfvrsn=5b518b38_3 "View the Delaware Women's Suffrage Monument Booklet")
  * [Women’s Service monument dedication booklet](https://legis.delaware.gov/docs/default-source/default-document-library/delawarewomensservicemonumentbook-reprint05-2025.pdf?sfvrsn=b4508b38_3 "View the Delaware Women's Service Monument Booklet")


### Capitol Decorum
  * Visitors should keep in mind that this is a working Capitol.
  * Cameras are allowed in the Capitol tour area but not in the Chambers when the Legislature is in session.
  * Capitol Police will strictly enforce all safety and security guidelines.


### Parking
Parking is available in the Delaware Public Archives, the Tatnall Building, and the Del-One Federal Credit Union lots. Parking is limited on session days. Handicapped parking and handicapped access are located on the east side of the building. If you need directions, please visit our [Hours and Directions](https://legis.delaware.gov/Resources/HoursAndDirections) page.
### Visiting the Capitol
Visitors to the Capitol must use the west door. The handicapped entrance is located on the east side of the building.
### Smoking Policy
Please be advised, there is no smoking permitted on any state grounds or state facility, including vaping.
### Kiosk Access
A Kiosk is located in the main lobby.
### Cafeteria
The Legislative Hall Café is located on the ground floor of Legislative Hall. Visit the [information page](https://legis.delaware.gov/LegislativeHallCafe "Legislative Hall Cafeteria Information") for hours and menus. 
Vending machines are also located in the cafeteria.
Seating can be limited on session days. Joint Finance and Bond Committee Hearings are televised in the cafeteria. 
### Restrooms
Restroom facilities are located on all three floors. All public facilities are handicapped accessible.
  * [About Legislative Hall](https://legis.delaware.gov/Resources/AboutLegislativeHall)
  * [Hours and Directions](https://legis.delaware.gov/Resources/HoursAndDirections)

## Session Info
**Live session proceedings and committee hearings, as well as their recordings are viewable from the[Live Stream Page](https://sg001-harmony.sliq.net/00329/Harmony/en/View/UpcomingEvents/20240109/-1 "Click to go to the Live Stream pag").  
**
  * _The[**House**](https://legis.delaware.gov/Events/Agenda/House "Click to view the House Agenda") is in session on Tuesdays, Wednesdays, and Thursdays from   
04/14/2026 to 04/23/2026.  
_
  * _The __**[Senate](https://legis.delaware.gov/Events/Agenda/Senate "Click to view the Senate Agenda")**__ is _in _session on Tuesdays, Wednesdays, and Thursdays from  
_04/14/2026 to 04/23/2026.____


_Information to[register for e-mail notifications](https://legis.delaware.gov/Resources/DE_NotificationService "Register for e-mail notifications") on legislation and committee meetings.

### Visiting Legislative Hall
Legislative Hall is located at:   
411 Legislative Avenue   
Dover, DE 19901   
  
[Legislative Hall Cafeteria](https://legis.delaware.gov/LegislativeHallCafe "Click to view information on the Legislative Hall Cafeteria")  
  
__For questions or assistance please call 302-744-4114 or email ____DGA_ __Reception@delaware.gov_____ _.__  
  
Want to know more about Legislative Hall? [Learn about the rich history of the Delaware State House](https://legis.delaware.gov/Resources/History "History of the State House").

### Looking for Help?
Every day, your legislative staff helps constituents solve issues they encounter ranging from potholes in their streets to animal-related concerns.
We're happy to help direct constituents to proper forms, facilitate communications with other state and city departments, and advocate on behalf of our constituents.
[View Common Constituent Issues](http://legis.delaware.gov/Offices/ConstituentAssistance)  
  

### Budget and Bond Bills
Please visit the [Current Appropriations Bills](https://legis.delaware.gov/Offices/ControllerGeneral/AppropriationBills) page to see the current fiscal year's Operating and Capital Budget Bills.   
  
To submit comments on the budget or bond bills, click here.
### Grant-In-Aid Information
Grant-In-Aid is an appropriation made by the General Assembly to support the activities of non-profit organizations which provide services to the citizens of Delaware.
[Get More Information on Grant-In-Aid](http://legis.delaware.gov/GrantInAid)
### Report
Delaware Department of Labor and Delaware Department of Finance Report to the Delaware General Assembly regarding financial irregularities at the Department of Labor's Division of Unemployment Insurance  
  
[Unemployment Insurance Irregularity Report_July2024](https://legis.delaware.gov/docs/default-source/reports/dol_dofreporttoleadersofgeneralassembly_7-30-24.pdf?sfvrsn=53748838_2)
### Redistricting Information
Redistricting is the process of drawing new district boundaries for congressional, legislative and state school board districts based on each State's resident population.   
  
Please visit the [Redistricting Information page](https://legis.delaware.gov/Redistricting "Click for additional information on Redistricting") for more information.

Dover, DE 19901

## Office of the Chief Clerk of the House
The Chief Clerk is the chief administrative officer of the House of Representatives. A full-time employee, the Chief Clerk serves all forty-one members of the House. Primary duties include numbering and printing of all legislation introduced, recording all votes taken on the House floor and certifying the daily House Journal. The Chief Clerk is the chief parliamentarian and advises the Speaker of the House on parliamentary matters.
### Office Hours
**Monday** 8:30 AM - 4:30 PM  
**Tuesday** 8:30 AM - 4:30 PM  
**Wednesday** 8:30 AM - 4:30 PM  
**Thursday** 8:30 AM - 4:30 PM  
**Friday** 8:30 AM - 4:30 PM  
**Saturday** Closed  
**Sunday** Closed  
  
Hours may vary on Legislative Session Days as the Office of the Chief Clerk serves at the pleasure of the House of Representatives. 
### Have a Question
Richard Puffer, Chief Clerk  
Delaware House of Representatives  
email: richard.puffer@delaware.gov
  * **Office of the Chief Clerk of the House**

    * [House Journal](https://legis.delaware.gov/Chambers/House/Journal)
    * [House Voting Records](https://legis.delaware.gov/Chambers/House/RollCall)

## Office of the Secretary of the Senate
The Secretary of the Senate is the chief administrative officer of the Senate. The Secretary is a full-time staff official elected by the members through resolution and is administered an oath of office. The Secretary consults regularly with the President Pro Tempore on matters relating to budget, legislation and overall operations of the Senate.   
  
The Office of the Secretary maintains records of official Senate transactions, handles the introduction and flow of legislation, send and receive legislative messages and executive communications, compiles and posts agendas, records committee reports, roll calls and the legislative journal. The Office of the Secretary assists the members and their offices with various matters as requested and is often the point of initial enquiry and direction from the public and within the legislature.
### Office Hours
**Monday** 9:00 AM - 5:00 PM  
**Tuesday** 9:00 AM - 5:00 PM  
**Wednesday** 9:00 AM - 5:00 PM  
**Thursday** 9:00 AM - 5:00 PM  
**Friday** 9:00 AM - 5:00 PM  
**Saturday** Closed  
**Sunday** Closed  
  
Hours may vary on Legislative Session Days as the Office of the Secretary serves at the pleasure of the Delaware State Senate.
### Have A Question
Ryan Dunphy  
Secretary, Delaware State Senate  
  
phone: (302) 744-4129  
fax: (302) 739-7718  
email: Ryan.Dunphy@delaware.gov  

  * Office of the Secretary of the Senate

## Rules of the House
The House Rules are the procedures the House follows. The House Rules include procedures on committees, the conduct of Representatives, and how bills and resolutions are voted on. The House voted to adopt their Rules on 1/14/2025 by passing [House Resolution 3](https://legis.delaware.gov/BillDetail?LegislationId=141781).  
  
We have created guides on some of the House Rules, which can be accessed below. Questions on the House Rules can be directed to the [Chief Clerk of the House](https://legis.delaware.gov/Chambers/House/OfficeOfTheChiefClerkOfTheHouse). 
  * **[House Rules](https://legis.delaware.gov/docs/default-source/house/houserules.pdf?sfvrsn=c4cb8838_1 "House Rules")**  
  

  * **[General& Floor Procedures](https://legis.delaware.gov/docs/default-source/house/housegeneralfloorprocedures.pdf?sfvrsn=99cb8838_1 "House General & Floor Procedures")  
  
**
  * **[Committee Procedures](https://legis.delaware.gov/docs/default-source/house/housecommitteeprocedures.pdf?sfvrsn=98cb8838_1 "House Committee Procedures")  
**  

  * **[What to Say and When to Say It](https://legis.delaware.gov/docs/default-source/house/housewhattosayandwhentosayit.pdf?sfvrsn=49c88838_1 "House What to Say and When to Say It")**
